Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO MRN: V001111342 FIN: V[PHONE-29]
Age: 39 Years Sex: Male DOB: [DOB-1463]
Chief Complaint
MVA this morning. right side low back pain, neck pain, right shoulder and knee pain.
passenger in car where car was hit. denies hitting head, LOC, blood thinners
History of Present Illness
39-year-old male patient no significant past medical or surgical history presents to the
ED today with right-sided shoulder pain, neck pain, low back pain and right pain. 
Patient was a restrained passenger when the vehicle he was traveling in was by another
vehicle traveling about 3035 mph. Damage was noted to the passenger door and
passenger rear door. Patient was traveling in a midsize SUV.
He was able to self extricate. No complaints during the event. He complains of pain
this morning worse with movement.
He denies any headache. He did not strike his head. He does have left-sided trapezial
neck pain worse with movement and worse when he moves his left shoulder.
No obvious deformity or swelling noted on my exam today. No seatbelt sign today
Physical Exam
Vitals & Measurements
T: 98.2 °F (Oral) T: 36.8 °C TMIN: 98.2 °F (Oral) TMAX: 36.8 °C 
HR: 80 (Peripheral) RR: 16 BP: 132/86 SpO2: 98% WT: 109.09 kg (Dosing) BMI: 
32.6
General: Alert and oriented, well nourished, no acute distress.
Neurologic: Awake, alert, and oriented X3, CN II-XII intact.
Eye: PERRL, EOMI, normal conjunctiva.
HENT: Normocephalic, clear tympanic membranes, normal hearing, moist oral mucosa,
no scleral icterus, no sinus tenderness.
Medications
No qualifying data available

Emergency
Neck: Supple, non-tender, no carotid bruits, no JVD, no lymphadenopathy.
Lungs: Clear to auscultation and percussion, non-labored respiration.
Heart: Normal rate, regular rhythm, no murmur, gallop or edema.
Abdomen: Soft, non-tender, non-distended, normal bowel sounds, no masses.
Musculoskeletal: Normal range of motion and strength, no tenderness or swelling.
Skin: Skin is warm, dry and pink, no rashes or lesions.
Psychiatric: Cooperative, appropriate mood and affect.
Medical Decision Making
39-year-old male patient no significant past medical or surgical history presents to the
ED today with right-sided shoulder pain, neck pain, low back pain and right pain. 
Patient was a restrained passenger when the vehicle he was traveling in was by another
vehicle traveling about 30-35 mph. Damage was noted to the passenger door and
passenger rear door. Patient was traveling in a midsize SUV.
No seatbelt sign today noted. No chest pain or shortness of breath. No tenderness to
his abdomen. We will perform x-rays to rule out any acute bony abnormality however I
suspect this is more musculoskeletal.
We will treat his pain with IM Toradol and reassess. Reassessment reveals pain is
improved.
X-rays today reveal no acute bony abnormality. He does have some degenerative
changes however no acute findings noted today. Today he will be discharged home
with muscle relaxants and knee with new or worsening symptoms. We discussed
implementing heat therapy.
Impression and Disposition
1. Motor vehicle accident
Ordered:
ibuprofen(ibuprofen 600 mg oral tablet), 600 mg= 1 Tab, Oral, Q8H
methocarbamol(Robaxin 500 mg oral tablet), 500 mg= 1 Tab, Oral, TID
Discharge, Start: 06/30/25 14:28:00 EDT, Discharge to: Home
2. Musculoskeletal pain
Ordered:
ibuprofen(ibuprofen 600 mg oral tablet), 600 mg= 1 Tab, Oral, Q8H
methocarbamol(Robaxin 500 mg oral tablet), 500 mg= 1 Tab, Oral, TID
Discharge, Start: 06/30/25 14:28:00 EDT, Discharge to: Home
Discharge Follow Up
 Follow up with primary care provider - Within 2 to 3 days

Emergency
If no medications are listed here, you did not have any recorded medications as part of your stay and your provider has not prescribed
any new medications as part of your discharge.
The home medications listed are only as accurate as the information you provided. Please continue taking all of your medications
prescribed by your Primary Care Provider unless specifically told to change or discontinue the medication. Please direct any questions
regarding your home medications to your Primary Care Provider.
Take your medications faithfully. Do NOT skip medication. Do NOT stop taking medications without the direction of a health care
provider. Carry a list of your medications with you at all times, and take this medication list with you to your first follow up visit. Report
any side effects. Avoid herbal remedies unless discussed with your provider.
As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and
driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or
questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time,
which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Education Materials
Muscle Pain, Adult
Muscle pain, also called myalgia, is a condition in which a person has pain in one or more muscles in the body. The pain may be mild,
moderate, or severe. It may feel sharp, achy, or burning. In most cases, the pain lasts only a short time and goes away on its own.
It is normal to feel some muscle pain after you start a new exercise program. Muscles that have not been used a lot will be sore at first.
What are the causes?
You may have muscle pain when you use your muscles in a new or different way after not having used them for some time. Muscle pain
can also be caused by overuse or by stretching a muscle beyond its normal length (muscle strain). You may be more likely to have
muscle pain if you are not in shape.

Report Request ID: 264775602 [DOB-1289] 11:20 EDT
Emergency
Other causes may include:
• Injury or bruising.
• Infectious diseases. These include diseases caused by viruses, such as the flu (influenza).
• Fibromyalgia. This is a long-term (chronic) condition that causes muscle tenderness, tiredness (fatigue), and headache.
• Autoimmune or rheumatologic diseases. These are conditions, such as lupus, that cause the body's defense system (immune
system) to attack areas in the body.
• Certain medicines. These include ACE inhibitors and statins.
What are the signs or symptoms?
The main symptom is sore or painful muscles. Your muscles may be sore when you do activities and when you stretch. You may also
have slight swelling.
How is this diagnosed?
Muscle pain is diagnosed with a physical exam. Your health care provider will ask questions about your pain and when it began.
• If you have not had muscle pain for very long, your provider may want to wait before doing much testing.
• If your muscle pain has lasted a long time, tests may be done right away.
• In some cases, you may need tests to rule out other conditions and diseases.
How is this treated?
Treatment for muscle pain depends on the cause. Home care is usually enough to relieve the pain. Your provider may also prescribe
NSAIDs, such as ibuprofen.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your provider.
• Ask your health care provider if the medicine prescribed to you requires you to avoid driving or using machinery.
Managing pain, swelling, and discomfort

Report Request ID: 264775602 [DOB-1283] 11:20 EDT
Emergency
• If told, put ice on the painful area for the first 2 days of soreness.
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.
—46 If your skin turns bright red, remove the ice right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of damage is higher if you
cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
• For the first 2 days of muscle soreness, or if there is swelling:
—46 Do not soak in hot baths.
—46 Do not use a hot tub, steam room, sauna, heating pad, or other heat source.
• After 2-3 days, you may switch between putting ice and heat on the area. If told, apply heat to the affected area as often as
told by your provider. Use the heat source that your recommends, such as a moist heat pack or a heating pad.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the heat source.
—46 Leave the heat on for 20–30 minutes.
• If your skin turns bright red, remove the ice or heat right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of damage is higher if you
cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
• If you have an injury, raise (elevate) the injured area above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down.
Activity
• If your muscle pain is caused by overuse:
—46 Slow down your activities until the pain goes away.
—46 Do regular, gentle exercises if you are not normally active.
—46 Warm up before you exercise. Stretch before and after you exercise. This can help lower the risk of muscle pain.
• Do not keep working out if the pain is severe. Severe pain could mean that you have injured a muscle.
• You may have to avoid lifting. Ask your provider how much you can safely lift.
• Return to your normal activities as told by your provider. Ask your provider what activities are safe for you.

MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital

MRN: V001111342 Account #: V[PHONE-1282]
Emergency
If told, put ice on the painful area for the first 2 days of soreness.
46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
-46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2-3 times a day.
-46 If your skin turns bright red, remove the ice right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of damage is higher if you
cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
For the first 2 days of muscle soreness, or if there is swelling:
46 Do not soak in hot baths.
-46 Do not use a hot tub, steam room, sauna, heating pad, or other heat source.
After 2-3 days, you may switch between putting ice and heat on the area. If told, apply heat to the affected area as often as
told by your provider. Use the heat source that your recommends, such as a moist heat pack or a heating pad.
46 Place a towel between your skin and the heat source.
-46 Leave the heat on for 20-30 minutes.
If your skin turns bright red, remove the ice or heat right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of damage is higher if you
cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
If you have an injury, raise (elevate) the injured area above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down.

46 Slow down your activities until the pain goes away.

Report Request ID: 264775602 [DOB-187] 11:20 EDT
Emergency
General instructions
• Do not use any products that contain nicotine or tobacco. These products include cigarettes, chewing tobacco, and vaping
devices, such as e-cigarettes. If you need help quitting, ask your provider.
Contact a health care provider if:
• Your muscle pain gets worse, and medicines do not help.
• The muscle pain lasts longer than 3 days.
• You have a rash or fever.
• You have muscle pain after a tick bite.
• You have muscle pain when you work out, even though you are in good shape.
• You have redness, soreness, or swelling.
• You have muscle pain after you start a new medicine or change the dose of a medicine.
Get help right away if:
• You have trouble breathing.
• You have trouble swallowing.
• You have muscle pain along with a stiff neck, fever, and vomiting.
• You have severe muscle weakness, or you cannot move part of your body.
• You are urinating less, or you have dark, bloody, or discolored urine.
• You have redness or swelling at the site of the muscle pain.
These symptoms may be an emergency. Get help right away. Call 911.
• Do not wait to see if the symptoms will go away.
• Do not drive yourself to the hospital.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.
Document Revised: [DOB-188] Document Reviewed: [DOB-189]

Muscle and Joint Pain: What It Means
Muscle and joint pain is aches and pains in your bones, joints, muscles, and tissues that surround them. This pain can happen in any
part of the body. It can last for a short time or a long time.
To find the cause of the pain, you may have:
• A physical exam.
• Lab tests.
• Imaging tests.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines

Emergency
• Take your medicines only as told.
• Treatment may include medicines for pain and inflammation.
• You might need to take medicines by mouth or put them on your skin.
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling
• Use ice or an ice pack as told.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the ice.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.
• Use heat as told.
—46 Use the heat source that your health care provider recommends, such as a moist heat pack or a heating pad. Do this
as often as told.
–52 Place a towel between your skin and the heat source.
–52 Leave the heat on for 20–30 minutes.
—46 If your skin turns red, take off the ice or heat right away to prevent burns. The risk of burns is higher if you can't feel
pain, heat, or cold.
Activity
• When your pain is very bad, bed rest may be helpful. Lie or sit in any position that's comfortable.
• Get up to take short walks at least every 2 hours during the day. This helps you breathe better and keeps your blood flowing.
Ask for help if you feel weak or unsteady.
• You may continue doing your usual activities unless the activities cause more pain.
• When the pain gets better, slowly increase the time and intensity of your activities or exercise.
Lifestyle

• Your provider may tell you to see a physical therapist to help you do exercises to improve movement and strength in the

• Your pain gets worse.

Elsevier Patient Education © 2024 Elsevier Inc.
Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult
After a car accident (motor vehicle collision), it is common to have injuries to your head, face, arms, and body. These injuries may
include cuts, burns, and bruises. The injuries may also include sore muscles, muscles strains, headaches, and broken bones.
You may feel stiff and sore for the first several hours. You may feel worse after waking up the first morning after the accident. These
injuries often feel worse for the first 24–48 hours. After that, you will usually begin to get better with each day. How quickly you get better
often depends on:
• How bad the accident was.
• How many injuries you have.
• Where your injuries are.
• What types of injuries you have.
• If you were wearing a seat belt.
• If your airbag was used.
A head injury may result in a concussion. This is a type of brain injury that can have serious effects. If you have a concussion, you
should rest as told by your doctor. You must be very careful to avoid having a second concussion.
Page 24 of 100
MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO DOB/Age/Sex: 3/27/1986 39 years Male

Emergency

Ask your provider if you should try:
46 Meditation or yoga.
-46 Therapy.
-46 Acupuncture or massage.

Your provider may tell you to see a physical therapist to help you do exercises to improve movement and strength in the
affected area.
Exercise as told.

You can't use the part of your body that hurts, such as your arm, leg, or neck.

You feel numb or you have tingling in the painful area.

have with your health care provider.

MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO DOB/Age/Sex: 3/27/1986 39 years Male

LEGEND: *=Corrected, @=Abnormal, C=Critical, L=Low, H=High, f=Footnote, #=Interpretive Data, R=Ref Lab
Report Request ID: 264775602 [DOB-1247] 11:20 EDT
Emergency
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor.
• If you were prescribed antibiotics, take or apply them as told by your doctor. Do not stop using them even if you start to feel
better.
Wound care
Follow instructions from your doctor about how to take care of your wound. Make sure you:
• Clean your wound. To do this:
—46 Wash it with mild soap and water.
—46 Rinse it with water to get all the soap off.
—46 Pat it dry with a clean towel. Do not rub it.
—46 Put an ointment or cream on the wound, if you were told to do so.
• Know when and how to change or remove your bandage (dressing).
• Always wash your hands with soap and water for at least 20 seconds before and after you change your bandage. If you
cannot use soap and water, use hand sanitizer.
• Leave stitches or skin glue in place for at least 2 weeks.
• Leave tape strips alone unless you are told to take them off. You may trim the edges of the tape strips if they curl up.
• Avoid getting sun on your wound.
• Do not disturb the wound. This means:
—46 Do not scratch or pick at the wound.
—46 Do not break any blisters you may have.
—46 Do not peel any skin.
Check your wound every day for signs of infection. Check for:
• More redness, swelling, or pain.
• More fluid or blood.
• Warmth.
• Pus or a bad smell.
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling

Emergency
• If told, put ice on the injured areas.
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.
—46 If your skin turns bright red, take off the ice right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of skin damage is higher if
you cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
• Raise (elevate) the wound above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down.
—46 Sleep with your head raised if the wound is on your face. You may do this by putting an extra pillow under your head.
Activity
• Rest. Rest helps your body to heal. Make sure you:
—46 Get plenty of sleep at night. Avoid staying up late.
—46 Go to bed at the same time on weekends and weekdays.
• You may have to avoid lifting. Ask your doctor how much you can safely lift.
• Ask your doctor when you can drive, ride a bicycle, or use machinery. Do not do these activities if you are dizzy.
• If you are told to wear a brace on an injured arm, leg, or other part of your body, follow instructions from your doctor about
activities. Your doctor may give you instructions about driving, bathing, exercising, or working.
General instructions
• If you have a splint, brace, or sling, follow your doctor's instructions on how to use the device.
• Drink enough fluid to keep your pee (urine) pale yellow.
• Do not drink alcohol.
• Eat healthy foods.
Contact a doctor if:
• You have very bad neck pain, especially pain in the middle of the back of your neck.
• You have loss of feeling (numbness), tingling, or weakness in your arms or legs.
• You have a change in your ability to control your pee or poop (stool).
• You have swelling in any area of your body, especially your legs.
• You have signs of infection in a wound.
• You have a fever.
• You have blood in your pee, poop, or vomit.
• You have any of the following symptoms for more than 2 weeks after your car accident:
—46 Long-term (chronic) headaches.

—46 Dizziness or balance problems.

Get help right away if:
• You have shortness of breath.
• You have light-headedness or you faint.
• You have chest pain.
• You have these eye or vision changes:
—46 Sudden vision loss or double vision.
—46 Your eye suddenly turns red.
—46 The black center of your eye (pupil) is an odd shape or size.
These symptoms may be an emergency. Get help right away. Call 911.
• Do not wait to see if the symptoms will go away.
• Do not drive yourself to the hospital.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms
Fatigue/being
tired Anxiety Back Pain
Chest pressure,
squeezing, or
discomfort
Shortness of
breath
Sweating, or a
cold sweat
Feeling of
impending
doom
There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.

at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes
Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol
Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
• 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
• 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1 PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2 PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.

Emergency
Behavioral / Mental Health Resources at UofL Health
If you or a loved one needs mental health, suicide, or substance use related crisis support, call or text 988
(1-[PHONE-260]) - National Suicide & Crisis Lifeline to connect with a trained crisis counselor. If this is a medical
emergency, dial 911. Walk-In assessments are welcome at all UofL Health Emergency Departments and UofL Health -
Peace Hospital.
UofL Health – UofL Hospital Emergency Psychiatric Services For questions or concerns, call [PHONE-1203].
Adults, may be:
• Discharged with an outpatient resource that is appropriate to their needs.
• Admitted to EPS’s Holding Bed Unit for observation or transferred to another hospital via ambulance.
• A team of psychiatrists, psychiatric nurse practitioners and social workers determine the best treatment options.
UofL Health – Mary & Elizabeth Hospital 
Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification from alcohol, opioids, benzodiazepines, and various other addictive
substances in a safe and monitored environment.
• Support groups, Group therapy, Certified peer support specialists.
• After care services and connecting patients with community resources.
• Alcoholic Anonymous (AA) meeting available onsite.
For Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification admission or services call [PHONE-1202].

Behavioral / Mental Health Resources at UofL Health
If you or a loved one needs mental health, suicide, or substance use related crisis support, call or text 988
(1-[PHONE-1198]) - National Suicide & Crisis Lifeline to connect with a trained crisis counselor. If this is a medical
emergency, dial 911. Walk-In assessments are welcome at all UofL Health Emergency Departments and UofL Health -
Peace Hospital.
UofL Health - UofL Hospital Emergency Psychiatric Services For questions or concerns, call [PHONE-267].
Adults, may be:
Discharged with an outpatient resource that is appropriate to their needs.
Admitted to EPS's Holding Bed Unit for observation or transferred to another hospital via ambulance.
A team of psychiatrists, psychiatric nurse practitioners and social workers determine the best treatment options.

Emergency
The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
I hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. I understand that I have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. I understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. I understand that I should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

(CR Knee AP LAT Oblique RT) PAIN
Report
INDICATION:
Neck, low back, right knee and right humerus pain. Motor vehicle accident today
COMPARISON:
None available.
FINDINGS/impression:
3 views right knee. No fracture. No dislocation or bone destruction.
4 views right humerus. No fracture. No dislocation. No bone destruction.
4 view cervical spine. Reversal of the cervical lordosis could be related to muscle spasm or positional. Minimal
degenerative change. Cervical bodies maintain normal height and otherwise alignment is preserved. Craniocervical
junction is intact.
3 views lumbar spine. Early degenerative changes. Lumbar vertebral bodies have normal height. Alignment is preserved.

USING AND SHARING MY INFORMATION
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 ("HIPAA").
This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients' treatment, contact, and financial
information. Taken together, this information is called your "Health Information". There are also other federal and/or
state laws that require Uofl Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of Health Information,
including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health; developmental disabilities;
treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and counseling; HIV/AIDS; sexual
assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic abuse of an adult with a disability;
child abuse and neglect.
Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices ("NPP"): If my permission is required by law, by signing this form I
agree that UofL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent and as set
forth in UofL Health's NPP. I understand that I can find more information about my rights to my Health Information,
and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, in the NPP. I acknowledge that if I requested a copy of the
NPP that I have been given a copy. I further understand that the NPP is available on UofL Health's website at:
www.uoflhealth.org.
I agree that my permission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health's possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
I understand that UofL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will protect or use my
information. I understand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: I understand that UofL Health may receive, use, and
disclose my Health Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use and disclose
my Health Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: I understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health information for
certain aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my care outside UofL
Health. If I desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, I must notify UofL Health's Health
Information Management Department by phone: [PHONE-938], option 2. I understand and agree that my request
will be evaluated to determine if it is reasonable and in the best interest of my health care to comply with my request.
I will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my request. If my request is granted and I
am are in need of emergency treatment, UofL Health may end the restriction if the information is needed to provide
my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more information on these types of uses and disclosures for
further information.)
Fundraising Activities: UofL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. I give my permission
to be contacted relating to fundraising opportunities. If I prefer not to be contacted about fundraising, 1 must notify
UofL Health by email to: [EMAIL-527] or by phone [PHONE-936]
Operational Purposes: I agree that the contact information I give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers and
email addresses, may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with me for
operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot reminders, and
patient surveys.

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
I understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. I hereby agree that the
difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if I request one at any
point during my stay.
I hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under any
applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my Authorized
Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that I may have under such insurance
policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to pursue such claim,
right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan, including the right and
ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by the provisions of the
Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
I also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan
documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisions, claims
for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute, administrative
hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health information to my
insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be involved in the resolution
of claims, in connection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4) receive any notices in connection
with my benefit claims or appeals concerning same.
If my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, I hereby waive any privilege I may have with UofL
Health, or other healthcare provider, and I hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's compensation
administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the event there is a
dispute about the compensability of my claim or worker's compensation benefits, and if my employer is not
specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's compensation medical
expenses for the condition or injury that is the basis of my admission, I agree to be personally responsible for all such
expenses. I further agree that, if my worker's compensation claim is settled with my employer on a disputed basis
without a specific finding that such is compensable as a worker's compensation injury, I (or my attorney, if I am
represented) will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to pay all amounts owed to UofL Health for treatment
of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and I hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of
all such expenses under such circumstances.
PERSONAL EQUIPMENT AND VALUABLES
I understand that UofL Health does not accept responsibility and will not reimburse me for the loss of money, jewelry,
eyewear, hearing aids, dentures, clothing or other personal property or valuables I bring to UofL Health. I take full
responsibility for such items and agree to release UofL Health from any and all liability from damage, loss or theft of
such items unless, as applicable, the items are deposited at UofL Health safe for safekeeping. I also understand that
I must inform a nurse if I bring any electrical equipment to UofL Health (e.g., home insulin pumps; BiPAP machine,
CPAP machine) and adhere to UofL Health policies regarding its use. I assume full responsibility for such electrical
equipment and for any injury caused by the use of the electrical equipment brought from home.
COMMUNICATIONS
By providing my cell, landline, or any other phone number(s), I expressly consent to receiving communications from
UofL Health, its staff, its contractors, collection agents, and others, at any numbers I provide or that are later
acquired for me. These parties may use this information to contact me by live agent, voice mail, text message, using
an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any other form of electronic
communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up health care reminders,
scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. I understand that depending on my
phone plan I could be charged for these calls or text messages. I agree to provide new number(s) if my number(s)
change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving healthcare services.

General Consent on Admission
The term "UofL Health" means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
I give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, I consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
I have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. I consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
I understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat me or have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. I also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. I further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians' assistants employed by physician
groups. I understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. I also understand that there may be medical students, medical and
surgical residents in various fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals are not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. I further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. I understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under a contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors' actions by providing this
service.
I understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and I have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
I understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, I may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic purposes. I also
understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as an emergency worker,
fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although 1 will be informed of the right to consent to testing for HIV or
other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be performed on previously gathered
bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
I agree that 1 obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of UofL Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. I also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or other
sources.
1 understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health's charges for any reason, or if I have no
insurance, I will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health's charges. I am aware that I must
notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if I believe I may qualify for financial assistance.
I/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL Health or to the
physicians providing Services at UofL Health. I understand they will bill my insurance directly for their Services, at a
rate not to exceed the UofL Health's or physician's regular charges. Insurance includes but is not limited to, my
medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan, accident, worker's compensation
benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or underinsured insurance

General Consent on Admission
The term "UofL Health" means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
I give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, I consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
I have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. I consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
I understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat me or have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. I also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. I further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians' assistants employed by physician
groups. I understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. I also understand that there may be medical students, medical and
surgical residents in various fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals are not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. I further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. I understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under a contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors' actions by providing this
service.
I understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and I have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
I understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, I may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic purposes. I also
understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as an emergency worker,
fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although 1 will be informed of the right to consent to testing for HIV or
other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be performed on previously gathered
bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
I agree that 1 obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of UofL Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. I also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or other
sources.
1 understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health's charges for any reason, or if I have no
insurance, I will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health's charges. I am aware that I must
notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if I believe I may qualify for financial assistance.
I/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL Health or to the
physicians providing Services at UofL Health. I understand they will bill my insurance directly for their Services, at a
rate not to exceed the UofL Health's or physician's regular charges. Insurance includes but is not limited to, my
medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan, accident, worker's compensation
benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or underinsured insurance

If no medications are listed here, you did not have any recorded medications as part of your stay and your provider has not prescribed
any new medications as part of your discharge.
The home medications listed are only as accurate as the information you provided. Please continue taking all of your medications
prescribed by your Primary Care Provider unless specifically told to change or discontinue the medication. Please direct any questions
regarding your home medications to your Primary Care Provider.
Take your medications faithfully. Do NOT skip medication. Do NOT stop taking medications without the direction of a health care
provider. Carry a list of your medications with you at all times, and take this medication list with you to your first follow up visit. Report
any side effects. Avoid herbal remedies unless discussed with your provider.
As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and
driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or
questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time,
which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Emergency
Behavioral Health Resources 
If you need behavioral health support, or are worried about someone else, please contact the Suicide & Crisis Lifeline by calling
1-[PHONE-928] or by texting or calling 9-8-8.
 
UofL Health – Peace Hospital
No charge level-of-care assessments. Walk-ins welcome at 2020 Newburg Road or any UofL Health emergency department. Inpatient
and intensive outpatient services are available.
Open 24/7 - [PHONE-929].
 
UofL – Department of Psychiatry
A full-service outpatient mental health practice serving adults. This respected group of physicians and therapists includes psychiatrists,
psychologists, psychiatric social workers, and addiction counselors.
Call office at [PHONE-930] to make an appointment.
 
UofL Trager Institute/Republic Bank Optimal Aging Clinic
Outpatient behavioral health is offered to individuals, couples, and families. The staff of licensed therapists are assisted by a team of
over 50 practicum students from the University of Louisville Schools of Social Work, Clinical Psychology, Clinical Behavioral Health, and
Nursing many who act as intern therapists providing free counseling to those that cannot afford a co-pay. Our students are all
supervised by licensed mental healthcare providers.
Call the office at [PHONE-931] or visit our website: https:// www.tragerinstitute.org/ mental-health-supports.
 
PeaceNow- Telebehavioral Health Clinic
Integrated telebehavioral health in primary care offices.
Includes:
• A telebehavioral health assessment of any patient (Adult/Adolescent/Child) by a licensed behavioral health clinician to determine
appropriate level of care.
• Brief teletherapy by a licensed clinician if recommended.
• Brief psychotropic medication management prescribed by a psychiatric nurse practitioner or psychiatrist if recommended.
• Resources plus referral for ongoing outpatient therapy and medication management if appropriate
To schedule an appointment with a primary care provider call [PHONE-932] or
visit https://uoflhealth.org/services/primary-care/.
 
For more information call, [PHONE-933].
 
Seven Counties Services
Provides outpatient therapy services and crisis stabilization.
24/7 Adult Crisis Line - [PHONE-934]
24/7 Child Crisis Line - [PHONE-935]
Outpatient Therapy-First Appointment- [PHONE-936]
Bipolar I Disorder
Bipolar I disorder is a mental health disorder in which a person has episodes of emotional highs (mania) and may also have episodes of
lows (depression). Bipolar I disorder differs from other bipolar disorders in that it involves extreme episodes of mania (manic episodes).
These episodes last at least one week or involve severe symptoms that require a hospital stay to keep the person safe.
What are the causes?
The cause of this condition is not known.
What increases the risk?

MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO DOB/Age/Sex: 3/27/1986 39 years Male
MRN: V001111342 Account #: V[PHONE-959]
LEGEND: *=Corrected, @=Abnormal, C=Critical, L=Low, H=High, f=Footnote, #=Interpretive Data, R=Ref Lab
Report Request ID: 264775601 [DOB-960] 11:19 EDT
Emergency
The following factors may make you more likely to develop this condition:
• Having a family member with the disorder.
• Having an imbalance of certain chemicals in the brain (neurotransmitters).
• Experiencing stress, such as from illness, financial problems, or a death.
• Having certain conditions that affect the brain or spinal cord (neurologic conditions).
• Having had a brain injury (trauma).
What are the signs or symptoms?
Symptoms of bipolar I disorder include the following:
Symptoms of mania
• Very high self-esteem or self-confidence.
• Less need for sleep.
• Unusual talkativeness. Speech may be very fast.
• Racing thoughts with quick shifts between topics that may or may not be related (flight of ideas).
• Being much more able or much less able to concentrate.
• Increased purposeful activity, such as work, studies, or social activity.
• Increased agitation. This could be pacing, squirming, fidgeting, or finger and toe tapping.
• Impulsive behavior and poor judgment. These may lead to high-risk activities that are sexual, financial, or physical.
Symptoms of depression
• Extreme sadness, uncontrollable crying, or feeling hopeless, worthless, or numb.
• Sleep problems, such as trouble falling asleep or staying asleep (insomnia), waking early, or sleeping too much.
• No longer enjoying things you used to enjoy.
• Isolation, or spending time alone often.
• Lack of energy or motivation, and moving more slowly than normal.
• Trouble making decisions.
• Increased appetite or loss of appetite.
• Thoughts of death, or wanting to harm yourself.
Sometimes, you may have a mixed mood. This means having symptoms of mania and depression at the same time. Stress can often
trigger these symptoms.
How is this diagnosed?
This condition may be diagnosed based on a mental health evaluation that includes a review of:
• Emotional episodes.
• Medical history.
• Use of alcohol, drugs, and prescription medicines. Certain medical conditions and substances can cause secondary bipolar
disorder. This has symptoms like the symptoms of bipolar disorder.
Your health care provider may ask you to take a short test to help understand your symptoms. You may also be asked to follow up with a
mental health provider for further evaluation or to start treatment.
Page 21 of 91
MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO DOB/Age/Sex: 3/27/1986 39 years Male
MRN: V001111342 Account #: V[PHONE-961]
Emergency
The following factors may make you more likely to develop this condition:
Having a family member with the disorder.
Having an imbalance of certain chemicals in the brain (neurotransmitters).
Experiencing stress, such as from illness, financial problems, or a death.
Having certain conditions that affect the brain or spinal cord (neurologic conditions).
Having had a brain injury (trauma).
What are the signs or symptoms?
Symptoms of bipolar I disorder include the following:
Symptoms of mania
Very high self-esteem or self-confidence.
Less need for sleep.
Unusual talkativeness. Speech may be very fast.
Racing thoughts with quick shifts between topics that may or may not be related (flight of ideas).
Being much more able or much less able to concentrate.
Increased purposeful activity, such as work, studies, or social activity.
Increased agitation. This could be pacing, squirming, fidgeting, or finger and toe tapping.
Impulsive behavior and poor judgment. These may lead to high-risk activities that are sexual, financial, or physical.
Symptoms of depression
Extreme sadness, uncontrollable crying, or feeling hopeless, worthless, or numb.
Sleep problems, such as trouble falling asleep or staying asleep (insomnia), waking early, or sleeping too much.
No longer enjoying things you used to enjoy.
Isolation, or spending time alone often.
Lack of energy or motivation, and moving more slowly than normal.
Trouble making decisions.
Increased appetite or loss of appetite.
Thoughts of death, or wanting to harm yourself.
Sometimes, you may have a mixed mood. This means having symptoms of mania and depression at the same time. Stress can often
trigger these symptoms.
How is this diagnosed?
This condition may be diagnosed based on a mental health evaluation that includes a review of:
Emotional episodes.
Medical history.
Use of alcohol, drugs, and prescription medicines. Certain medical conditions and substances can cause secondary bipolar
disorder. This has symptoms like the symptoms of bipolar disorder.
Your health care provider may ask you to take a short test to help understand your symptoms. You may also be asked to follow up with a
mental health provider for further evaluation or to start treatment.

MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: GODSEY JR, CHARLES LEO DOB/Age/Sex: 3/27/1986 39 years Male

LEGEND: *=Corrected, @=Abnormal, C=Critical, L=Low, H=High, f=Footnote, #=Interpretive Data, R=Ref Lab
Report Request ID: 264775601 [DOB-966] 11:19 EDT
Emergency
How is this treated?
This condition is a long-term (chronic) illness. It is often managed with ongoing treatment rather than treatment only when symptoms
occur. A combination of treatments is often used. Treatment may include:
• Medicines, usually medicines called mood stabilizers. Medicines can be prescribed by a health care provider who specializes
in treating mental health disorders (psychiatrist). If symptoms occur during use of a mood stabilizer, other medicines may be
added.
• Talk therapy (psychotherapy) to help you manage bipolar disorder. Talk therapy includes cognitive behavioral therapy (CBT)
and family therapy.
• Psychoeducation. This helps you and others understand how your disorder is managed. Include friends and family in
educational sessions so they learn how best to support you.
• Methods of managing your condition, such as journaling or relaxation exercises. Exercises include:
—46 Yoga.
—46 Meditation.
—46 Deep breathing.
• Lifestyle changes, such as:
—46 Limiting alcohol and drug use.
—46 Exercising regularly.
—46 Setting a regular bedtime and wake time.
—46 Eating a healthy diet.
• Electroconvulsive therapy (ECT). This is a procedure in which electricity is applied to the brain through the scalp. ECT may be
used for severe bipolar disorder when medicine and psychotherapy work too slowly or do not work.
Follow these instructions at home:
Activity
• Return to your normal activities as told by your health care provider.
• Find activities that you enjoy, and make time to do them.
• Get regular exercise.
Lifestyle

Emergency
• Follow a set schedule for eating and sleeping.
• Eat a healthy diet that includes fresh fruits and vegetables, whole grains, low-fat dairy, and lean meat.
• Get at least 7–8 hours of sleep each night.
• Avoid using products that contain nicotine or tobacco. If you want help quitting, ask your health care provider.
• Avoid alcohol and drugs. They can affect how medicine works and make symptoms worse.
General instructions
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider. You may think about stopping your
medicine, but you need to take all your medicine as prescribed. This helps manage your symptoms.
• Consider joining a support group. Your health care provider may be able to recommend one.
• Talk with your family and friends about your treatment goals and how loved ones can help.
• Keep all follow-up visits. This is important.
Where to find more information
• National Alliance on Mental Illness: nami.org
• National Institute of Mental Health: nimh.nih.gov
Contact a health care provider if:
• Your symptoms get worse, or your loved ones tell you that your symptoms are getting worse.
• You have uncomfortable side effects from your medicine.
• You have trouble sleeping.
• You have trouble doing daily activities.
• You feel unsafe in your surroundings.
• You are using alcohol or drugs to manage your symptoms.
Get help right away if:
• You have new symptoms.
• You have thoughts about harming yourself or others.
• You are considering suicide.

Emergency
If you ever feel like you may hurt yourself or others, or have thoughts about taking your own life, get help right away. Go to
your nearest emergency department or:
• Call your local emergency services (911 in the U.S.).
• Call a suicide crisis helpline, such as the National Suicide Prevention Lifeline at 1-[PHONE-979] or 988 in the U.S.
This is open 24 hours a day in the U.S.
• If you’re a Veteran:
—46 Call 988 and press 1. This is open 24 hours a day.
—46 Text the Veterans Crisis Line at 838255.
Summary
• Bipolar I disorder is a lifelong mental health disorder in which a person has episodes of mania and depression.
• Treatment for this disorder involves a combination of treatments such as medicines and talk and behavioral therapies.
• Include friends and family in educational sessions so they know how best to support you.
• Get help right away if you are considering suicide.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Emergency
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms
Fatigue/being
tired Anxiety Back Pain
Chest pressure,
squeezing, or
discomfort
Shortness of
breath
Sweating, or a
cold sweat
Feeling of
impending
doom
There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure
Family History Obesity Age
Gender (Males are
at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes
Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol
Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.

MEH Mary and Elizabeth Hospital

Report Request ID: 264775601 [DOB-999] 11:19 EDT
Emergency
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
• 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
• 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1 PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2 PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
3 KNOW THE
SYMPTOMS
• Confusion or
disorientation
• Shortness of breath
• High heart rate
• Fever, shivering, or
feeling very cold
• Extreme pain or
discomfort
• Clammy or sweaty
skin

Emergency
Why Hands-Only CPR?
Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!

Emergency
Behavioral / Mental Health Resources at UofL Health
If you or a loved one needs mental health, suicide, or substance use related crisis support, call or text 988
(1-[PHONE-1012]) - National Suicide & Crisis Lifeline to connect with a trained crisis counselor. If this is a medical
emergency, dial 911. Walk-In assessments are welcome at all UofL Health Emergency Departments and UofL Health -
Peace Hospital.
UofL Health – UofL Hospital Emergency Psychiatric Services For questions or concerns, call [PHONE-1013].
Adults, may be:
• Discharged with an outpatient resource that is appropriate to their needs.
• Admitted to EPS’s Holding Bed Unit for observation or transferred to another hospital via ambulance.
• A team of psychiatrists, psychiatric nurse practitioners and social workers determine the best treatment options.
UofL Health – Mary & Elizabeth Hospital 
Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification from alcohol, opioids, benzodiazepines, and various other addictive
substances in a safe and monitored environment.
• Support groups, Group therapy, Certified peer support specialists.
• After care services and connecting patients with community resources.
• Alcoholic Anonymous (AA) meeting available onsite.
For Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification admission or services call [PHONE-1014].
Adult Medical Behavioral Health Unit can provide treatment and care for medically compromised patients.
Behavioral health services include:
• Acute crisis stabilization, treatment of acute psychiatric symptoms
• Group/individual therapy
• Behavior and medical management
For Adult Medical Behavioral Health Unit services or information about admission, please call [PHONE-1015]. 
UofL Health – Peace Hospital Open 24/7 at 2020 Newburg Rd., Louisville, KY 40205 – [PHONE-1016]). 
 
Treatment for psychiatric and substance use disorders.

Outpatient behavioral health is offered to individuals, couples, and families. 
• Free counseling to those that cannot afford a co-pay. 
• 14 years old and above (select therapists).

PeaceNow: Tele-behavioral Health Clinic For more information call [PHONE-1035]
A Tele-behavioral health assessment for adults or adolescents (age 12 and above) by a licensed behavioral health
clinician to determine an appropriate level of care. 
• Brief teletherapy by a licensed mental health clinician (if recommended). 
• Psychotropic medication management prescribed by a psychiatric nurse practitioner or psychiatrist (if
recommended). 
• Resources plus referral for ongoing outpatient therapy and medication management(if appropriate).

Emergency
The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
I hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. I understand that I have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. I understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. I understand that I should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

General Consent on Admission
The term "UofL Health" means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
I give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, I consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
I have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. I consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
I understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat me or have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. I also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. I further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians' assistants employed by physician
groups. I understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. I also understand that there may be medical students, medical and
surgical residents in various fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals are not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. I further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. I understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under a contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors' actions by providing this
service.
I understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and I have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
I understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, I may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic purposes. I also
understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as an emergency worker,
fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although I will be informed of the right to consent to testing for HIV or
other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be performed on previously gathered
bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY
I agree that I obligate myself and/or the Patient to pay the account(s) of UofL Health in accordance with the
established rates and payment policy of UofL Health. I also understand that patient/guarantor payments can be
applied to any account where payment is due to include any credit balance resulting from benefit payments or other
sources.
I understand that if my Insurer denies all or any part of UofL Health's charges for any reason, or if I have no
insurance, I will be personally and fully responsible for payment of UofL Health's charges. I am aware that I must
notify the Business Office and submit the completed application form if I believe I may qualify for financial assistance.
I/My Designated Health Care Representative authorizes billing by and direct payment to UofL Health or to the
physicians providing Services at UofL Health. I understand they will bill my insurance directly for their Services, at a
rate not to exceed the UofL Health's or physician's regular charges. Insurance includes but is not limited to, my
medical health insurance policy/policies, including my employee health benefit plan, accident, worker's compensation
benefits, motor vehicle insurance, casualty insurance, and uninsured or underinsured insurance

General Consent on Admission
The term "UofL Health" means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
I give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, I consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
I have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. I consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
I understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat me or have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. I also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. I further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians' assistants employed by physician
groups. I understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. I also understand that there may be medical students, medical and
surgical residents in various fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals are not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. I further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. I understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under a contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors' actions by providing this
service.
I understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and I have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
I understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, I may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic purposes. I also

bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
